          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          across different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is
          critical for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association
          studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes in
          disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
          architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
          play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
          introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation is
          base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
          same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed

      response:
        output: >-
          Genes operate in concert within specific contexts to carry out their
          functions. To understand how these genes impact complex traits, it is
          essential to comprehend the regulation of gene expression across
          various conditions. This understanding has been proven crucial in
          developing new therapeutic strategies. Transcriptome-wide association
          studies have been instrumental in revealing the role of individual
          genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of
          complex trait architecture suggest that interactions between genes are
          vital for disease onset and progression. In this paper, we present
          PhenoPLIER, a computational method that consolidates gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified
          latent representation for a combined analysis. This representation is
          based on modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns under
          identical conditions. We find that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. Our
          method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we discovered that functionally significant players, while
          lacking associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can provide context to genetic associations and
          uncover potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. Thus,
          PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic
          associations through the perspective of gene modules.

          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").

      response:
        output: >-
          In the realm of functional genomics, understanding how genes interact
          in different contexts to influence complex traits is crucial,
          particularly for developing new therapies. Despite advances in
          transcriptome-wide association studies, which have shed light on the
          roles of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, a gap
          remains in comprehending the significance of gene-gene interactions in
          disease origin and progression. This study introduces PhenoPLIER, a
          computational approach designed to fill this gap. PhenoPLIER maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          shared latent representation for a joint analysis, based on modules of
          genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our
          findings reveal that diseases are significantly associated with gene
          modules expressed in relevant cell types. Furthermore, PhenoPLIER
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of
          action. A CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation further
          underscores the importance of this approach, as it reveals that
          functionally significant players, although lacking associations, are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Ultimately,
          PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic
          associations through the lens of gene modules, thereby illuminating
          potential therapeutic targets overlooked by single-gene strategies and
          advancing our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

      response:
        output: >-
          The intricate interplay of genes in specific contexts is pivotal to
          their functionality, and understanding this complex relationship is
          critical for the development of new therapies. While
          transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role of
          individual genes in disease mechanisms, current models suggest that
          gene-gene interactions are central to disease onset and progression, a
          nuanced aspect that remains largely unexplored. This paper introduces
          PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach designed to bridge this gap
          by mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a shared latent representation for combined analysis, based
          on modules of genes expressing similar patterns across identical
          conditions. Our results indicate that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
          PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Moreover, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid
          regulation reveals that functionally significant players, although
          lacking associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER offers a novel perspective for
          interpreting genetic associations, highlighting the potential of
          co-expressed gene groups and revealing potential targets overlooked by
          single-gene strategies, thereby advancing our understanding of genetic
          interactions in disease mechanisms.

          Genes operate in concert within specific contexts to fulfill their
          functions. A mechanistic comprehension of gene expression regulation
          across varying conditions is essential to understand how these genes
          influence complex traits. This understanding is crucial for the
          development of new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies

          to disease. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture
          suggest that interactions between genes play a pivotal role in the
          onset and progression of diseases. In this study, we introduce

        output: >-
          In the broader field of functional genomics, understanding how genes
          influence complex traits has been a persistent challenge due to the
          intricate interplay of gene-gene interactions across diverse
          conditions. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed
          light on individual gene roles in disease mechanisms, the current
          understanding of complex traits architecture suggests that
          interactions between genes are pivotal in disease onset and
          progression, a gap not yet fully addressed. Herein, we introduce
          PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that bridges this gap by
          mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data
          into a unified latent representation based on modules of co-expressed
          genes. Our results indicate that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER has
          demonstrated its precision in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. In a case study employing a CRISPR
          screen for lipid regulation analysis, we found that PhenoPLIER
          prioritizes functionally important players that lack associations but
          are highlighted in trait-associated modules. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
          offers a significant advancement in interpreting genetic associations
          by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, thus revealing
          potential therapeutic targets overlooked by single-gene strategies.
          This innovative approach has the potential to reshape our
          understanding of complex trait architecture and expedite the discovery
          of new therapeutic targets and drug repurposing opportunities.

          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        output: >-
          In the field of genetics, understanding how genes interact in specific
          contexts to influence complex traits is crucial for developing new
          therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed
          light on the role of individual genes, modern models suggest that
          gene-gene interactions are key to disease origin and progression, a
          gap yet to be fully explored. This study introduces PhenoPLIER, a
          computational approach that bridges this gap by mapping gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. This innovative method is
          based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the
          same conditions. Our results show that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
          PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers
          mechanisms of action. Additionally, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid
          regulation revealed that functionally important players lacking
          associations were prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating groups of
          co-expressed genes, provides a novel framework for interpreting
          genetic associations, revealing potential targets missed by
          single-gene strategies and advancing our understanding of disease
          mechanisms.

          Genes operate synergistically within specific contexts to execute
          their functions. A mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation
          across varying conditions is crucial to understand how these genes
          impact complex traits. Such understanding is vital for the development
          of new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have
          illuminated the role of individual genes in disease-related
          mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture
          suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal to the onset and
          progression of diseases. We present PhenoPLIER, a computational method

          predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.

          revealed that functionally important elements, though lacking
          associations, are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating groups of
          co-expressed genes, can contextualize genetic associations and uncover
          potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. Therefore,
          PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic
          associations through the perspective of gene modules.

          In the realm of functional genomics, understanding the intricate
          interactions of genes and their role in complex traits is pivotal,
          necessitating a comprehensive grasp of gene expression regulation
          across varying conditions. This understanding is integral to the
          development of novel therapies. While transcriptome-wide association
          studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease
          mechanisms, current models suggest that gene-gene interactions are
          instrumental in disease onset and progression - an aspect that remains
          inadequately explored. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a

          PhenoPLIER, by integrating groups of co-expressed genes, offers a
          fresh perspective on interpreting genetic associations, potentially
          unveiling therapeutic targets overlooked by single-gene strategies.
          This novel approach propels the field of functional genomics forward,
          providing a new lens through which to view genetic associations in the
          context of gene modules.

          Within the broader field of genomics, the intricate interplay of
          gene-gene interactions and their role in complex traits is an area
          rich for exploration. Despite advances in transcriptome-wide
          association studies, which have elucidated the role of individual
          genes in disease mechanisms, there remains a gap in our understanding
          of how gene-gene interactions influence disease origin and
          progression. Our research aims to fill this gap by introducing
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data for a comprehensive
          analysis. PhenoPLIER operates on a novel principle of mapping these
          associations into a common latent representation, based on modules of
          co-expressed genes across various conditions. Our results indicate a
          significant correlation between diseases and gene modules expressed in
          relevant cell types, with PhenoPLIER accurately predicting known
          drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Further
          validation using a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation revealed that
          PhenoPLIER could prioritize functionally important players that lack
          direct associations but are included in trait-associated modules. In
          conclusion, PhenoPLIER offers a new perspective for interpreting
          genetic associations, emphasizing the importance of gene modules over
          single-gene strategies. This innovative approach not only enhances our
          understanding of gene-gene interactions and complex traits but also
          holds potential for identifying previously overlooked therapeutic
          targets.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript. Revise the following abstract of
          this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure and fits in
          a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          Within the broader field of genetic research, understanding how genes
          interact to influence complex traits is essential, particularly in the
          context of disease origin and progression. While transcriptome-wide
          association studies have shed light on the role of individual genes,
          current models suggest a critical role for gene-gene interactions, a
          facet not yet fully explored. This gap in our understanding hinders
          the development of new therapies, necessitating a more comprehensive
          approach. To address this, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
          method that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a unified latent representation for joint
          analysis. This approach is based on modules of genes that exhibit
          similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our findings
          demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with gene
          modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately
          predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
          Through the application of a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation
          analysis, we discovered that functionally important genes, previously
          overlooked due to lack of associations, are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by
          focusing on groups of co-expressed genes, provides a novel way to
          interpret genetic associations, revealing potential targets missed by
          single-gene strategies. This finding has significant implications for
          advancing our understanding of genetic interactions and their role in
          disease progression.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in

          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        output: >-
          While recent genetic studies and transcriptome-wide association
          studies have greatly advanced our understanding of the role individual
          genes play in disease mechanisms, a significant gap remains in our
          understanding of how gene-gene interactions contribute to disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms. This lack of insight into the complex
          architecture of these traits hinders our ability to develop effective
          therapies. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
          computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent representation
          for joint analysis. This approach is unique in that it is based on
          modules of genes with similar expression patterns across various
          conditions, thus capturing the complexity of gene-gene interactions.
          Our findings reveal that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER
          accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of
          action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we discovered that functionally important players,
          although lacking direct associations, are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These findings demonstrate
          that by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential therapeutic
          targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. Therefore, PhenoPLIER
          offers a significant advancement in functional genomics, providing a
          new framework for interpreting genetic associations and potentially
          accelerating drug repurposing and the identification of therapeutic
          targets.

          Within the broader field of genomics, a critical gap exists in

          Despite advances in understanding genetic associations and their role
          in disease etiology, a significant gap remains in our ability to
          unravel the complex interplay of gene-gene interactions and their
          impact on disease progression and drug mechanisms. This gap stems from
          the current focus on individual gene associations, overlooking the
          potential collective influence of gene modules, groups of genes with
          similar expression patterns across conditions. We address this gap
          with the introduction of PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach
          that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint
          analysis. Our approach leverages the concept that genes operate
          synergistically in specific contexts to perform their functions.
          PhenoPLIER is built on the premise of gene modules, which are
          significantly associated with diseases when expressed in relevant cell
          types. Our findings demonstrate that PhenoPLIER accurately predicts
          known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, it
          successfully prioritizes functionally important players in
          trait-associated modules, even those lacking direct associations, as
          evidenced by a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation. In
          conclusion, PhenoPLIER offers a significant step forward in the
          interpretation of genetic associations, highlighting the critical role
          of gene modules. By shifting the focus from individual genes to
          co-expressed gene groups, this approach has the potential to unearth
          novel therapeutic targets and advance drug repurposing efforts,
          thereby transforming our understanding of disease etiology and drug
          mechanisms.

          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          genes, can reveal potential therapeutic targets missed by single-gene
          strategies, advancing the field of drug repurposing and therapeutic

          contemporary models suggest that gene-gene interactions significantly
          impact disease origin and progression, a facet not fully explored in
          existing literature. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
          novel computational approach that amalgamates gene-trait associations
          and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent
          representation for comprehensive analysis. PhenoPLIER's unique
          representation is predicated on modules of genes that exhibit similar
          expression patterns across identical conditions. Our findings reveal
          that diseases are strongly linked to gene modules expressed in
          pertinent cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, our
          CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation indicates that PhenoPLIER
          prioritizes functionally important players in trait-associated
          modules, even when these players lack direct associations. In
          conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by integrating groups of co-expressed genes,
          provides a powerful tool for contextualizing genetic associations and
          identifying potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies.
          This innovative approach advances our understanding of genetic
          associations through the lens of gene modules, thereby propelling the
          field of complex trait research forward.

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript. Revise the following abstract of
          this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure and fits in
          a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          underexplored area, particularly in relation to expression regulation
          across varying conditions. This gap in knowledge holds significant
          implications for the development of new therapies. Our study addresses

          our results demonstrate that PhenoPLIER not only provides a fresh
          perspective for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of
          gene modules, but also uncovers potential targets that single-gene
          strategies may overlook, thus advancing the broader field of genetic
          research.

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript. Revise the following abstract of
          this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure and fits in
          a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          Within the broader field of genetic research, a critical gap exists in
          understanding how genes collectively influence complex traits across
          various conditions, a knowledge crucial for developing new therapeutic
          strategies. Our research addresses this gap by introducing a novel
          approach, PhenoPLIER, which incorporates groups of co-expressed genes
          to contextualize genetic associations. Our study demonstrates that
          diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in
          relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known
          drug-disease pairs while inferring mechanisms of action. Notably, our
          findings from a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation reveal that
          key functional players, though lacking direct associations, are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion,
          our research illustrates that PhenoPLIER can reveal potential targets
          overlooked by single-gene strategies, providing a new framework for
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.
          This advancement significantly contributes to the field by enhancing
          our mechanistic understanding of gene expression regulation, thereby
          paving the way for the development of more effective therapies.

          improving the text of a manuscript. Revise the following abstract of
          this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure and fits in
          a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          In the field of genetics, understanding the collaborative roles of
          genes in specific contexts is imperative for deciphering their
          influence on complex traits and developing new therapies. However, a
          significant gap exists in our mechanistic understanding of how gene
          expression is regulated across different conditions. Addressing this
          gap, our study introduces a novel approach, PhenoPLIER, which
          incorporates groups of co-expressed genes to contextualize genetic
          associations. Our results demonstrate that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types.
          Furthermore, PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs
          and infers mechanisms of action. Notably, in a CRISPR screen analysis
          of lipid regulation, functionally important players lacking
          associations were prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER not only fills the existing gap
          in interpreting genetic associations but also unveils potential
          targets overlooked by single-gene strategies, thereby advancing the
          broader field of genetics.

          In the realm of genetic studies and functional genomics, understanding
          the co-expression of genes under varying conditions is essential for
          discerning their influence on complex traits and disease etiology.
          Although transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the
          role of individual genes, contemporary models suggest that gene-gene
          interactions are pivotal in disease onset and progression. However, a
          gap exists in our ability to effectively map these interactions and
          their pharmacological implications. To address this, we present
          PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that amalgamates gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified
          latent representation, based on modules of genes exhibiting similar
          expression patterns across identical conditions. Our results reveal a
          significant association of diseases with gene modules expressed in
          relevant cell types. Moreover, PhenoPLIER demonstrates accuracy in
          predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
          action. An additional application of our approach in a CRISPR screen
          for lipid regulation highlighted functionally important players that
          were previously overlooked in associations but were prioritized in
          trait-associated modules. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER fills a critical
          gap in the field, enhancing our understanding of disease etiology,
          drug mechanisms, and potential therapeutic targets, thus paving the
          way for drug repurposing and improved clustering of complex traits.

      prompt:
        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure
          and fits in a single paragraph. The revision should follow a
          context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The context
          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/prompts/candidate_with_metadata.txt
      vars: *ref_58
      response:
        output: >-
          While genes are known to interact in specific contexts to perform
          their functions, understanding how these interactions influence
          complex traits necessitates a deep comprehension of gene expression
          regulation across varying conditions, a crucial factor in developing
          new therapies. Although transcriptome-wide association studies have
          shed light on the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms,
          modern models of complex traits highlight the importance of gene-gene
          interactions in disease onset and progression, an area that remains
          underexplored. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
          computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent representation
          for a comprehensive analysis. This representation is founded on
          modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns across
          identical conditions. Our results reveal a significant association
          between diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types,
          demonstrating PhenoPLIER's accuracy in predicting known drug-disease
          pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Moreover, a CRISPR screen
          analysis of lipid regulation reveals that functionally important
          genes, though lacking associations, are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These findings not only answer
          the question of gene-gene interactions in disease development but also
          underscore the potential of PhenoPLIER as a tool for identifying
          therapeutic targets and advancing drug repurposing, thereby pushing
          the boundaries of functional genomics.

          portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The
          first sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
          which the manuscript's research is situated. Then, the context is
          narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
          answers. A successful context section distinguishes the research’s
          contributions from the current state-of-the-art, communicating what is
          missing in the current literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
          that matters (i.e. the connection between the specific gap and the
          broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g. "here we") first
          describes the novel method or approach that was used to fill the gap,
          then presents an executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion
          portion interprets the results to answer the question that was posed
          at the end of the context portion. There may be a second part to the
          conclusion portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the
          broader field forward (e.g. "broader significance").

          While it is well established that genes operate synergistically in
          specific contexts to fulfill their roles, the mechanistic
          understanding of their expression regulation across varying conditions
          remains a challenge for elucidating complex traits and developing new
          therapies. Despite transcriptome-wide association studies shedding
          light on individual gene roles in disease mechanisms, current models
          of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene interactions are
          pivotal in disease onset and progression. This study introduces
          PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that bridges this gap by
          mapping gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data
          into a unified latent representation for comprehensive analysis. This
          representation is grounded on modules of genes exhibiting similar
          expression patterns under identical conditions. Our findings reveal a
          significant association between diseases and gene modules expressed in
          relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease
          pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR
          screen to assess lipid regulation, we discovered that functionally
          crucial players, although lacking associations, are prioritized in
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. These findings underscore the
          potential of PhenoPLIER in identifying therapeutic targets and
          advancing drug repurposing, thereby contributing to the broader field
          of functional genomics and complex trait clustering.

          Within the broader field of gene expression regulation, the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms has been elucidated
          through transcriptome-wide association studies. However, a gap exists
          in our understanding of how gene-gene interactions contribute to

          identifying potential therapeutic targets, thus advancing the field of
          gene expression regulation.

          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/prompts/candidate.txt

      response:
        output: >-
          Within the broader field of genomics, the interplay of genes and their
          collective influence on complex traits is a critical area of study,
          particularly for the development of new therapies. While
          transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role of
          individual genes in disease mechanisms, the current literature lacks
          comprehensive models that account for gene-gene interactions, which
          are predicted to be pivotal in disease origin and progression. To fill
          this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that
          amalgamates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a unified latent representation for joint analysis. This
          innovative method hinges on the identification of gene modules, groups
          of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns under identical
          conditions. Our results reveal significant associations between
          diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER
          proves accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and deducing
          mechanisms of action. Moreover, a CRISPR screen analysis of lipid
          regulation indicates that while some functionally important genes lack
          direct associations, they are prioritized in trait-associated modules
          by PhenoPLIER. This conclusion not only answers the initial question
          of gene-gene interactions in disease progression but also advances the
          broader field by providing a novel approach to understanding complex
          trait architecture and disease mechanisms.

        - raw: >-
            You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
            improving the text of a manuscript with title '{{ title }}' and
            keywords '{{ keywords }}.' Revise the following abstract of this
            manuscript so that it has a clear sentence structure and fits in a
            single paragraph. The revision should follow a
            context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme, as follows: 1) The
            context portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will
            fill. The first sentence orients the reader by introducing the
            broader field in which the manuscript's research is situated. Then,
            the context is narrowed until it lands on the open question that the
            research answers. A successful context section distinguishes the
            research’s contributions from the current state-of-the-art,
            communicating what is missing in the current literature (i.e., the
            specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the connection between the
            specific gap and the broader context). 2) The content portion (e.g.
            "here we") first describes the novel method or approach that was
            used to fill the gap, then presents an executive summary of results.
            3) The conclusion portion interprets the results to answer the
            question that was posed at the end of the context portion. There may
            be a second part to the conclusion portion that highlights how this
            conclusion moves the broader field forward (e.g. "broader
            significance").

              Genes operate in concert within specific contexts to carry out
              their functions. To understand how these genes impact complex
              traits, it is essential to comprehend the regulation of gene
              expression across various conditions. This understanding has been
              proven crucial in developing new therapeutic strategies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in
              revealing the role of individual genes in disease-related
              mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait
              architecture suggest that interactions between genes are vital for
              disease onset and progression. In this paper, we present
              PhenoPLIER, a computational method that consolidates gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified
              latent representation for a combined analysis. This representation
              is based on modules of genes exhibiting similar expression
              patterns under identical conditions. We find that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types. Our method accurately predicts known drug-disease
              pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR
              screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discovered that
              functionally significant players, while lacking associations, are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER can provide context to genetic associations and uncover
              potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. Thus,
              PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the perspective of gene modules.

              distinguishes the research’s contributions from the current
              state-of-the-art, communicating what is missing in the current
              literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the
              connection between the specific gap and the broader context). 2)
              The content portion (e.g. "here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that was used to fill the gap, then presents an
              executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion portion interprets
              the results to answer the question that was posed at the end of
              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


              Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in
              specifico contexts to perform their functions. Determining how
              these genes influence complex traits requires a mechanistic
              understanding of expression regulation across different
              conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical for
              developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
              have helped uncover the role of individual genes in
              disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
              architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
              play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. This
              representation is base on modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are
              significantl associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules.

              In the field of genetics, understanding how genes interact in

              models suggest that gene-gene interactions are key to disease

              associations were prioritized in trait-associated modules by

              co-expressed genes, provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations, revealing potential targets missed by
              single-gene strategies and advancing our understanding of disease
              mechanisms.

              associations, potentially unveiling therapeutic targets overlooked

              to view genetic associations in the context of gene modules.

              therapeutic targets.

              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological

              combined analysis. It is well-understood that genes interact

              discerning these interactions in relation to complex traits

              PhenoPLIER offers an innovative framework for understanding

              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes
              exhibiting similar expression patterns across shared conditions.
              Our results show that diseases are significantly associated with
              gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. PhenoPLIER is also
              accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Moreover, by applying PhenoPLIER to a CRISPR
              screen for lipid regulation, we discovered that functionally
              important players lacking associations are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by
              incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, provides a new
              framework for interpreting genetic associations, contextualizes
              genetic associations, and uncovers potential targets missed by
              single-gene strategies, thereby advancing our understanding of
              complex trait architecture and disease progression.

              ---

              We present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational method that
              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a unified latent representation for
              combined analysis. Genes function collaboratively within specific
              contexts to carry out their roles. To understand how these genes
              affect complex traits, it is essential to grasp the regulation of
              expression across varying conditions. Such understanding is
              pivotal for the creation of new therapies. Transcriptome-wide
              association studies have been instrumental in elucidating the
              roles of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms.
              Nevertheless, contemporary models of complex trait architecture
              suggest that interactions between genes are vital to the onset and
              progression of diseases. PhenoPLIER's representation hinges on
              modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns under the
              same conditions. We have identified significant associations
              between diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell
              types. Our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
              infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, a CRISPR screen
              analysis of lipid regulation revealed that functionally
              significant elements lack associations but are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER,
              by incorporating clusters of co-expressed genes, can provide
              context to genetic associations and uncover potential targets that
              single-gene strategies may overlook. Thus, PhenoPLIER offers a
              fresh approach to interpreting genetic associations through the
              perspective of gene modules.

              role in disease etiology, a significant gap remains in our ability

              a shared latent representation for joint analysis. Our approach
              leverages the concept that genes operate synergistically in

              on the premise of gene modules, which are significantly associated
              with diseases when expressed in relevant cell types. Our findings

              prioritizes functionally important players in trait-associated
              modules, even those lacking direct associations, as evidenced by a

              of genetic associations, highlighting the critical role of gene
              modules. By shifting the focus from individual genes to
              co-expressed gene groups, this approach has the potential to
              unearth novel therapeutic targets and advance drug repurposing

              context portion communicates to the reader what gap the paper will
              fill. The first sentence orients the reader by introducing the
              broader field in which the manuscript's research is situated.
              Then, the context is narrowed until it lands on the open question
              that the research answers. A successful context section
              distinguishes the research’s contributions from the current
              state-of-the-art, communicating what is missing in the current
              literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e. the
              connection between the specific gap and the broader context). 2)
              The content portion (e.g. "here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that was used to fill the gap, then presents an
              executive summary of results. 3) The conclusion portion interprets
              the results to answer the question that was posed at the end of
              the context portion. There may be a second part to the conclusion
              portion that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader
              field forward (e.g. "broader significance").


              Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
              that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
              data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis.
              Genes act in concert with each other in specific contexts to
              perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence
              complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. It has been shown that
              this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of
              genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions.
              We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene
              modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
              accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

              ---

              We present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational method that
              integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data for a comprehensive joint analysis. Recognizing
              that genes operate synergistically within specific contexts, we
              aim to elucidate how these interactions influence complex traits
              by examining expression regulation under varying conditions. This
              understanding is essential for the development of new therapies.
              While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on
              the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, contemporary
              models of complex trait architecture suggest that gene-gene
              interactions are pivotal in disease onset and progression.
              PhenoPLIER's framework is grounded in modules of genes exhibiting
              similar expression patterns under identical conditions. We find
              that diseases have significant associations with gene modules
              expressed in pertinent cell types. Our method demonstrates
              accuracy in predicting established drug-disease pairs and deducing
              mechanisms of action. By employing a CRISPR screen to investigate
              lipid regulation, we discovered that functionally significant
              players, though lacking associations, are prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER
              enhances the interpretation of genetic associations by
              incorporating co-expressed gene groups, thereby unveiling
              potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
              thus offers a unique approach for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules.

              The field of genetic studies is increasingly recognizing the
              importance of understanding gene-gene interactions and their
              influence on complex traits, which is key to developing new
              therapies. Despite advances in transcriptome-wide association
              studies, a gap remains in our ability to fully capture the complex
              architecture of these traits, particularly in relation to disease
              origin and progression. To address this, we introduce PhenoPLIER,
              a novel computational approach that bridges this gap by mapping
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Our method is
              based on modules of genes that display similar expression patterns
              across various conditions, thereby enabling a more comprehensive
              understanding of gene interactions. We found that diseases are
              significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach accurately predicted known
              drug-disease pairs and inferred mechanisms of action. Notably, our
              CRISPR screen analysis of lipid regulation revealed that
              PhenoPLIER can prioritize functionally important genes that lack
              associations but are included in trait-associated modules. In
              conclusion, PhenoPLIER offers a significant advancement in
              interpreting genetic associations, contextualizing them through
              the lens of co-expressed gene modules. This approach not only
              fills a critical gap in our understanding of complex trait
              architecture, but also opens new avenues for identifying potential
              therapeutic targets overlooked by single-gene strategies.

              ---

              We present PhenoPLIER, a computational method that integrates
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data for
              joint analysis. Genes, acting in synchrony within specific
              contexts, perform their functions. A mechanistic understanding of
              gene expression regulation across varying conditions is crucial to
              ascertain how these genes influence complex traits. This
              understanding is vital for the development of new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role
              of individual genes in disease mechanisms. However, contemporary
              models of complex trait architecture suggest that interactions
              between genes are critical to the initiation and progression of
              diseases. PhenoPLIER's representation hinges on modules of genes
              that exhibit similar expression patterns under the same
              conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated
              with gene modules expressed in pertinent cell types. Our method
              accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms
              of action. Additionally, a CRISPR screen analyzing lipid
              regulation reveals that crucial functional components lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER, by incorporating clusters
              of co-expressed genes, can contextualize genetic associations and
              uncover potential targets overlooked by single-gene strategies.
              PhenoPLIER thus offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the perspective of gene modules.
